<div id="review_1171404066" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1171404066" />
    <a title="Candi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3639005-candi"><img alt="Candi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585187464p2/3639005.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1171404066?book_show_action=true">Jan 17, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Candi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Candi" href="/user/show/3639005-candi">Candi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780062285515" href="/book/show/22535477-the-enchanted">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3639005-candi?shelf=magical-realism">magical-realism</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1171404066" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11367108910927089389"><i>“For us, time doesn’t exist. The measurements of life – birth, death, loss, marriage, love, lust, happiness – have no meaning in this dungeon. Time passes here, but it doesn’t count. I could have a clock, but what would the dial tell me? Nothing. When time no longer exists, you don’t care about getting up, you don’t think about birthdays, you don’t think back to people you lost. You float free in the universe, untethered to anyone or anything. Your heart is empty, and because your heart is empty</i></span>
  <span id="freeText11367108910927089389" style="display:none"><i>“For us, time doesn’t exist. The measurements of life – birth, death, loss, marriage, love, lust, happiness – have no meaning in this dungeon. Time passes here, but it doesn’t count. I could have a clock, but what would the dial tell me? Nothing. When time no longer exists, you don’t care about getting up, you don’t think about birthdays, you don’t think back to people you lost. You float free in the universe, untethered to anyone or anything. Your heart is empty, and because your heart is empty, you have no time. You have no place in the universe. At least I used to think this way. Only listening to the lady and the priest has made me feel a little different. I think more about time now. Not for me but for the lady.”</i><br /><br />So says the narrator of this very powerful and intense book set in one of the darkest of places – the death row of an antiquated stone prison. Told through the first-person “voice” of a condemned man who has committed heinous and indescribable crimes, <b>The Enchanted</b> is simultaneously heartrending, hopeful and beautiful. As one would expect, the subject matter is often unsettling; however, the author does not go over the top with extreme and graphic images. Denfeld conveys to the reader the very real and ugly side to lives filled with physical, sexual, and mental abuse, the consequences of such horrors, and ultimately the atrocities of prison life itself; but she does so in an unusually quiet manner. <br /><br />The Lady, unnamed in this novel, is an attorney-hired investigator tasked with searching for information that could save the lives of death row inmates once their execution dates have been set. Sometimes successful and occasionally not, the Lady is confronted with a most difficult and rare case – that of York, who does not wish to be saved from death. Through her research, the Lady again confronts the misery of her own past which is not so different from that of York’s. This gives the Lady a unique perspective and perhaps an additional passion to help York and men like him. Her inclination to truly listen helps York open up and speak to her. <i>“The words tumble out as rough as rocks, but they are soon worn smooth, and more and more he hears himself talking – blessed surcease, a person just to listen to me – and the vowels round and the consonants grow into planets that become the universe that expands in the light in her dark eyes. She hears me, he thinks wildly – she hears me.”</i><br /><br />Throughout the novel, the reader also feels the raw pain of other damaged individuals such as the fallen priest in need of love and forgiveness, the white-haired boy who is a victim of the system and a recipient of the awful abuse within the prison walls, and the warden tormented by the anguish of his wife’s illness and impending death. And then, of course, we are always brought back to the narrator and his own inner turmoil. Described as a monster as a result of his crimes, the narrator manages the confusion and heartache of his past and the fears of everyday prison life by reading books and creating an imaginative world full of “enchantment”, running horses with <i>“gold-flecked nostrils and bronzed skin”</i>, tiny men with hammers within the walls, and other such fantasies. The reader in me could not help but delight in and identify with his love for books. <i>“After a time, it seemed that the world inside the books became my world. So when I thought of my childhood, it was dandelion wine and ice cream on a summer porch, like Ray Bradbury, and catching catfish with Huck Finn. My own memories receded and the book memories became the real memories, far more than the outside, far more even than in here.”</i> In a sense, books were his salvation. But, I think too, that the Lady was his salvation as well. Through his eyes we see her develop a relationship with the fallen priest, we see her deal with her own demons and nightmares of her past, and like the narrator, we gain a sense of hope that one can rise above the unthinkable miseries of a damaging childhood. <i>“The lady is like me in many ways. Serpents crawl inside her. She is deathly afraid that others will see them. She is afraid, and yet she wants the priest to see inside her and accept the monsters that wrap around the secret, pure part of her – the part she managed to save, miraculously, that so many of us have lost. She knows the monsters are there and yet wants to be seen. Her courage frightens and amazes me. It makes me hopeful for her. It makes me crave happiness for her. Is that what you call love? Is that what you call hope?”</i><br /> <br />Thought-provoking, simply but hauntingly beautiful, and with a perfect ending, <b>The Enchanted</b> is one you should not miss. I highly recommend this book that gets 4.5 stars from me. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11367108910927089389" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7555122-laura?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer971458163" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9850465601655602078">I don't think I've ever read a book with so many broken people. I think that some readers are going to say that the author is promoting propaganda but I think she was sharing with us a different take on humanity. She shares with us a side to these individuals that we could not possibly think are human. It's not promoting crimes without punishment but to maybe take a step back to see why someone commits such unspeakable crimes. The book spoke to me about a broken world that exists with real evil </span>
  <span id="freeText9850465601655602078" style="display:none">I don't think I've ever read a book with so many broken people. I think that some readers are going to say that the author is promoting propaganda but I think she was sharing with us a different take on humanity. She shares with us a side to these individuals that we could not possibly think are human. It's not promoting crimes without punishment but to maybe take a step back to see why someone commits such unspeakable crimes. The book spoke to me about a broken world that exists with real evil and real people struggling. You see into the lives of the lady, the priest, and the warden all struggling with their own brokenness, hurts, scars and regrets. There's a lot going on in this book and the author writes in a way you don't want to stop reading regardless of how difficult the scenarios are. I hope this isn't the last fictional book this author attempts bc she is truly a gifted fictional writer. <br /><br />Reading again for the 2nd time for book club...still tough.<br /><br />Reread for neighborhood book club: This book still strips you down even knowing the entire plot. This book makes you ask questions and think about some hard subjects. You can't help but to feel so many emotions while reading this book. I am anxious to see how book club members respond and are affected. Can a book like this be a glimpse of redemption? Please <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/56358.Rene_Denfeld" title="Rene Denfeld" rel="nofollow noopener">Rene Denfeld</a> give us another novel. <br /><br />Update:new novel on the way Sept 2017. Very excited!</span>

<div id="review_885795244" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer885795244" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13481024533306050167"><b> The Enchanted by Rene Denfeld.</b> <b> 2.5 Stars </b><br/><br/>Let me start my review by saying <u> I wanted</u> very badly to <u> love</u> this book like all my friends on Goodreads that have read it and have been seduced by it. To them I say.............I am <i> <b> Jealous</b> </i> of you all.<br/> I pre ordered my copy in Hardback as this was going to be one of those books that would not be borrowed under any circumstances and would remain on my book shelf for many years to come.<br/><br/>But unfortunately I wasn't enchanted or impressed by it and was l</span>
  <span id="freeText13481024533306050167" style="display:none"><b> The Enchanted by Rene Denfeld.</b> <b> 2.5 Stars </b><br /><br />Let me start my review by saying <u> I wanted</u> very badly to <u> love</u> this book like all my friends on Goodreads that have read it and have been seduced by it. To them I say.............I am <i> <b> Jealous</b> </i> of you all.<br /> I pre ordered my copy in Hardback as this was going to be one of those books that would not be borrowed under any circumstances and would remain on my book shelf for many years to come.<br /><br />But unfortunately I wasn't enchanted or impressed by it and was left feeling rather disappointed by much of the book and I will try and explain my reasons for my disappointment.<br /><br />First the book is set in an ancient stone prison somewhere in America and to begin with I was drawn into the story until the author introduced the magic realism aspect of the tale and I was completely thrown and just disconnected with the book completely. I don't get magic realism and I think being Irish may have been told too many stories of fairly forts and enchanted forests as child. <br /><br />I wanted to get to know the characters in this novel more and every time I thought I was getting the background information on one character (most of which remained nameless) I was thrown in a different direction. I found the fact that some of the characters remained nameless more distracting and confusing than an element of intrigue. I never seemed to get a sense of time or place from the novel and couldn't identity with the story as a result. I just finished the book feeling dissatisfied. <br /><br />Now I have to agree the prose is impressive and this author knows how to draw in her audience. As I said at the beginning I am envious of my friends who enjoyed this story and for anyone reading this review be assured my dislike of this story is based on the fact that I don't enjoy stories when magic realism is an element.<br /><br />And so this beautiful book will not sit on my book shelf :-( but rest assured all you lovers of The Enchanted I will endeavor to find a suitable home for it among my friends.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13481024533306050167" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1353042082" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1353042082" />
    <a title="Jennifer Masterson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28953843-jennifer-masterson"><img alt="Jennifer Masterson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600995952p2/28953843.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1353042082?book_show_action=true">Aug 02, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer Masterson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer Masterson" href="/user/show/28953843-jennifer-masterson">Jennifer Masterson</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1353042082" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer142990631735500244">I am late to the party on this book and I'm going to be the odd one out on "The Enchanted". Most people loved it but sadly not me. It is original and beautifully written but so so so dark that it didn't work for me. The magical realism with the subject matter I struggled with. <br/><br/>Don't take my word for it. Try It! It's a case of it's me not the book.</span>

<div id="review_1193520154" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1193520154" />
    <a title="Cathrine ☯️ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22600410-cathrine"><img alt="Cathrine ☯️ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582396518p2/22600410.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1193520154?book_show_action=true">Feb 07, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cathrine ☯️ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cathrine ☯️ " href="/user/show/22600410-cathrine">Cathrine ☯️ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/17936636-the-enchanted">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22600410-cathrine?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1193520154" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer656329389092239218"><b>5★</b><br/><i>“ Maybe we can stop men like me from happening. The lady has a gift, and I hope she keeps using it. It is the gift of understanding men like me.”</i><br/><br/>This book is compelling, haunting, mesmerizing, edgy, uncomfortable, unforgettable. I feel the need to find a Thesaurus to find words adequate enough to describe it. It immerses the reader in the pain of others causing one to rethink some ground rules you may have set for the limits of your compassion and does so with beautiful writing and pacing. Thi</span>
  <span id="freeText656329389092239218" style="display:none"><b>5★</b><br /><i>“ Maybe we can stop men like me from happening. The lady has a gift, and I hope she keeps using it. It is the gift of understanding men like me.”</i><br /><br />This book is compelling, haunting, mesmerizing, edgy, uncomfortable, unforgettable. I feel the need to find a Thesaurus to find words adequate enough to describe it. It immerses the reader in the pain of others causing one to rethink some ground rules you may have set for the limits of your compassion and does so with beautiful writing and pacing. Think of the most evil real life criminals guilty of unspeakable crimes against others and then imagine being a fly on the wall in their cells or seeing inside their twisted minds. This book is a virtual trip into their world. So dark yet not the nightmare I feared. By that I mean the author was very revealing, yet restrained. Reading it reminded me of Alfred Hitchcock’s genius of building almost unbearable suspense by pulling his audience into a film but allowing the space to use their own imagination; what one writer described as <i>“often inviting them to fill in the blanks."</i> There are the right amount of blanks in these pages. I feared it might be too gruesome and put off reading it for a long time based on that fear. <br /><br />How can I explain how awesome this book is; that I’m grateful to the author for composing something that reached my deepest humanity? It’s fiction based on fact because she’s <i>the lady</i> who has been there and knows that ugly and disturbing as it is, more people need to look more closely if we ever hope to have some answers and hope. No regrets here.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="656329389092239218" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_877486008" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/877486008" />
    <a title="Julie Christine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1213607-julie-christine"><img alt="Julie Christine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1445900882p2/1213607.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/877486008?book_show_action=true">Mar 10, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julie Christine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julie Christine" href="/user/show/1213607-julie-christine">Julie Christine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1213607-julie-christine?shelf=best-of-2014">best-of-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1213607-julie-christine?shelf=usa-contemporary">usa-contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1213607-julie-christine?shelf=contemporary-fiction">contemporary-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1213607-julie-christine?shelf=imagined-worlds">imagined-worlds</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1213607-julie-christine?shelf=read-2014">read-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1213607-julie-christine?shelf=social-political-commentary">social-political-commentary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer877486008" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10163024270589627612">Every once in a great while, a book enters my life and quick like ivy, its words and images rise and twist around my imagination and intellect. Rene Denfeld's extraordinary debut <i>The Enchanted</i> is one such book. I feel compelled to push it into everyone's hands, saying, "You must read this. You simply must." It's been nearly two years since the last time I read something that made me ache to shout it from the rooftops--another debut by an Oregon writer: Amanda Coplin's <i>The Orchardist</i>. Yet, these </span>
  <span id="freeText10163024270589627612" style="display:none">Every once in a great while, a book enters my life and quick like ivy, its words and images rise and twist around my imagination and intellect. Rene Denfeld's extraordinary debut <i>The Enchanted</i> is one such book. I feel compelled to push it into everyone's hands, saying, "You must read this. You simply must." It's been nearly two years since the last time I read something that made me ache to shout it from the rooftops--another debut by an Oregon writer: Amanda Coplin's <i>The Orchardist</i>. Yet, these two books could not be more dissimilar in style, content, and theme. <br /><br />I nearly set this aside after just a few pages. I will caution you. <i>The Enchanted</i> deals with the ugliest, most hopeless themes a writer can conjure: abuse, incest, rape, mental illness, murder. It is set in a prison. Two of its characters are on death row. <br /><br />And yet. <br /><br />Rene Denfeld works a kind of magic. This is a book of luminous and captivating prose and imagery, where angels of mercy shimmer in the darkest corners. Where horses gallop free, making the dripping, crumbling walls in the lowest level of this Gothic nightmare of a prison shudder and the warden laugh, even as he prepares a prisoner for his final moments on earth. <br /><br />The author seamlessly weaves multiple points of view and many richly drawn characters into a very few pages. The narrator is the only first-person perspective. He is the prison's most notorious death row resident, but his crimes remain untold. Mute, communicating only with the reader from the maze of his mind, this inmate views death row as sanctuary, its dank confines the only place he has found peace. <br /><br />Some characters are named: the prisoners York, Risk, Arden; Conroy, a brutal guard; Auntie Beth, a witness to a young boy's wretched upbringing. Other characters, whom we come to know intimately, painfully, remain only lower case titles: the warden; the priest; the white-haired boy. The lady. <br /><br />The lady. She is a death row investigator, like the author herself. Retained by York's attorneys, she is delving into the condemned's life, trying to uncover evidence that can be used to stay York's execution, to transmute his sentence from death to life. They share, as she learns, a similar horrific past. Yet, she became an angel-wounded, with broken wings- and he became a demon. York spurns her attempts to find mercy. He wants to die. <br /><br />Death is nearly as present a character as any living one in <i>The Enchanted</i> and the reader is reminded that we are all the walking dead, facing the same inevitable end as those on death row. Denfeld forces our moral hand, showing us all sides of the debate: the victims, the criminals, the decision-makers, and we are put in the uncomfortable position of empathizing with each. The warden, whose wife is in the end stages of cancer, contemplates the pro and anti death penalty protestors gathering outside his prison before an execution, and <br /><br /><blockquote>He wonders why so many easily accept death when it's caused by old age or cancer or even suicide, yet refuse to endorse death by execution. It seems wrong to him. No on deserves death more than someone like York or Striker or especially Arden. And yet those are the deaths that others will say are unnatural, not that of his dear sweet wide, a woman who raised three kids and never did anyone a wrong pass.</blockquote> <br />There are few writers who can wrest hope from the pit of horror with such eloquence. I think of Elie Wiesel and Primo Levi, who chronicled their Holocaust experiences, or Maya Angelou and Toni Morrison showing us the wretchedness of slavery and Jim Crow. These writers compel us to bear witness to humanity's darkest hours with beautiful language. With the same poignant but unsentimental style, Rene Denfeld applies a tender, humane voice to society's nightmares. She pries them open, releasing mystical creatures as symbols that help us understand our complex, real fears. <br /><br />Astonishing, original, terrible, and exquisite. It would not surprise me to see this nominated for book awards, and ranked high on critics' best of lists. It damn well better be. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10163024270589627612" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1372828890" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1372828890" />
    <a title="Ron" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43881851-ron"><img alt="Ron" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557265090p2/43881851.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1372828890?book_show_action=true">Aug 24, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ron" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ron" href="/user/show/43881851-ron">Ron</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1372828890" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12665768221261121106">I had not previously heard of The Enchanted before seeing it on a book club wall. I was interested, but not all that much, right? I really wasn’t expecting it to be this good.<br/><br/>Before reading, I had barely glanced at the jacket description. I do that sometimes because I just don’t want to know. Therefore, I had this idea going in that the building itself, housing the prisoners, was the “enchanted”, and hence the reason for the title. I figured we had a fantasy here of some sort. Well, I was wrong.</span>
  <span id="freeText12665768221261121106" style="display:none">I had not previously heard of The Enchanted before seeing it on a book club wall. I was interested, but not all that much, right? I really wasn’t expecting it to be this good.<br /><br />Before reading, I had barely glanced at the jacket description. I do that sometimes because I just don’t want to know. Therefore, I had this idea going in that the building itself, housing the prisoners, was the “enchanted”, and hence the reason for the title. I figured we had a fantasy here of some sort. Well, I was wrong. That happens a lot. To describe what the enchanted means in the book would probably spoil a few things, so I won’t.<br /><br />Rene Denfeld writing is almost lyrical, especially in areas of the book where she just lets it go. Within the seriousness of the story, there are elements of satire and of fantasy. At one point in the book, our unnamed narrator, a man waiting on death row in the dungeon of the building, feels the tremors of the golden horses beginning their run deep down in the earth below the dungeons. Denfeld doesn’t come out and tell us what these golden horses are; she lets the reader figure it out through the mind of the narrator. There are a handful of other characters at the center of the story; the lady, the fallen priest to name a couple of them. Each has a subplot that knits the whole story into one. <br /><br />I got to say that I almost gave it four stars because at times the prison is made out to be so bad it’s unreal. But then I remember it is a book of fiction meant to give a point and I get over myself. Can’t say it’s for everyone’s list, but I really liked it.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12665768221261121106" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/17936636-the-enchanted">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13400128-lynda?shelf=5-stars">5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13400128-lynda?shelf=mystery-thriller">mystery-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13400128-lynda?shelf=author-usa">author-usa</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13400128-lynda?shelf=z-read-2014">z-read-2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer811116097" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7555660061115047085"><b>"Back so long ago, when they built this enchanted place, they killed men in three ways: They waited for them to die, they worked them to death, and they hanged them. <br/><br/>Not much has changed. Instead of working men to death, there is a slow starvation of the body and soul. And instead of rope, they use a machine."</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/photos/1394381732p8/952720.jpg' width='400' height='200' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><blockquote>
  <b>"This is an enchanted place. Others don't see it, but I do."</b>
</blockquote><u>Publisher's synopsis</u><br/><blockquote>
  <i>The enchanted place is an ancient stone prison, viewed through the eyes of a death row inmate who find</i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText7555660061115047085" style="display:none"><b>"Back so long ago, when they built this enchanted place, they killed men in three ways: They waited for them to die, they worked them to death, and they hanged them. <br><br>Not much has changed. Instead of working men to death, there is a slow starvation of the body and soul. And instead of rope, they use a machine."</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/photos/1394381732p8/952720.jpg" width="400" height="200" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><blockquote>
  <b>"This is an enchanted place. Others don't see it, but I do."</b>
</blockquote><u>Publisher's synopsis</u><br><blockquote>
  <i>The enchanted place is an ancient stone prison, viewed through the eyes of a death row inmate who finds escape in his books and in re-imagining life around him, weaving a fantastical story of the people he observes and the world he inhabits. Fearful and reclusive, he senses what others cannot. Though bars confine him every minute of every day, he marries magical visions of golden horses running beneath the prison, heat flowing like molten metal from their backs, with the devastating violence of prison life.<br><br>Two outsiders venture here: a fallen priest, and the Lady, an investigator who searches for buried information from prisoners' pasts that can save those soon-to-be-executed. Digging into the background of a killer named York, she uncovers wrenching truths that challenge familiar notions of victim and criminal, innocence and guilt, honor and corruption-ultimately revealing shocking secrets of her own.</i>
</blockquote><u>Review</u><br><br>If there is one book that you simply must read over the course of 2014, it is The Enchanted. This is one of the most powerful, moving, haunting, intense, gut-wrenching, perplexing and captivating reads that I have experienced in a long, long time. I can not rate this book highly enough. 24 hours after having finished it I am still there, in the prison dungeons, listening, lurking, completely transfixed. <br><br>Written by Rene Denfeld, a fact investigator in death penalty cases, The Enchanted is a powerful book that gives death row a face. It is about characters whose lives intersect on death row; an inmate, an investigator and a chaplain, together with some strong secondary characters. <br><br>The story of each character individually is compelling, but they are interconnected so beautifully that they burst with emotion. The fluid prose that defines this novel is passionate and thought-provoking. Denfeld so artfully balances moments of stark sadness and cruelty, with such poignant images of beauty and grace.<br><br>Death row inmates deal with their demons in different ways. Some clutch their faith. Others draw or paint or write. Our narrator chooses to read voraciously and live in a fantasy world. <blockquote>
  <i>"The most wonderful enchanted things happen here - the most enchanted things you can imagine. I want to tell you while I still have time, before they close the black curtain and I take my final bow."</i>
</blockquote>Those on death row are convicted criminals; many are guilty of unspeakable cruelty and the most vicious of crimes. The Enchanted paints a picture of the 'person' and not just the crime for which they were committed. It explores the why. What made this person? Why did they do the things they did? What does it mean to be human?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/photos/1394383218p8/952735.jpg" width="400" height="200" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>He holds his fingers out of the cage. It is the eternal gesture of hope that says "touch me".</b><br><br>This book by design is intrusive and uncomfortable and challenges our core beliefs. But it is also beaufiful and breathtaking and simply enchanting. A must read for everyone. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/photos/1394383948p8/952739.jpg" width="150" height="50" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> 5/5 magical golden horses!</span>
  <a data-text-id="7555660061115047085" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9504700377883986823">I am kind of embarrassed - I really thought this was going to be a fantasy novel. I try to avoid reading the synopsis of books so that I am surprised - thus, I judged this book by its cover and it's name. <br/><br/>So, lemme tell you - this is not a fantasy novel! I would say that it is a cross between The Green Mile and The Shawshank Redemption. But, not quite as good.<br/><br/>I liked the story okay, but I am not sure I got what the author was trying to do with the way she wrote it. At times, I had trouble figuri</span>
  <span id="freeText9504700377883986823" style="display:none">I am kind of embarrassed - I really thought this was going to be a fantasy novel. I try to avoid reading the synopsis of books so that I am surprised - thus, I judged this book by its cover and it's name. <br /><br />So, lemme tell you - this is not a fantasy novel! I would say that it is a cross between The Green Mile and The Shawshank Redemption. But, not quite as good.<br /><br />I liked the story okay, but I am not sure I got what the author was trying to do with the way she wrote it. At times, I had trouble figuring out which character was the focus. Also, something about the way it was written got under my skin a little (just a tiny irritation, not something I can put my finger on, but it was not a comfortable read). Finally, there were some strange, unexplained occurrences that I kind of wanted explained - it didn't feel okay to me that I was left wondering what the heck happened.<br /><br />You may enjoy this book and you may not - enter at your own risk!</span>

<div id="review_920138238" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/920138238" />
    <a title="Carol" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7668522-carol"><img alt="Carol" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546364878p2/7668522.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/920138238?book_show_action=true">Apr 25, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carol" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carol" href="/user/show/7668522-carol">Carol</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780062285522" href="/book/show/18053078-the-enchanted">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7668522-carol?shelf=debut">debut</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7668522-carol?shelf=death">death</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7668522-carol?shelf=ebook">ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7668522-carol?shelf=read-2015">read-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7668522-carol?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7668522-carol?shelf=magical-realism">magical-realism</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer920138238" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17747603871471330782"><b>The Enchanted</b> is a dark and gloomy heartbreaking tale with just enough hope and magic to bring the reader back to the light, but <i>not</i> a book I would read again.<p>It is a story about the ugliness of prison life on Death Row, of living life in an evil underground dungeon. It is about black-shirted execution squads and corrupt guards who order young men in general population to the rape shed for personal gain, then call them used, broken and throwaways to break their spirit of any hope. It is about su</p></span>
  <span id="freeText17747603871471330782" style="display:none"><b>The Enchanted</b> is a dark and gloomy heartbreaking tale with just enough hope and magic to bring the reader back to the light, but <i>not</i> a book I would read again.<p>It is a story about the ugliness of prison life on Death Row, of living life in an evil underground dungeon. It is about black-shirted execution squads and corrupt guards who order young men in general population to the rape shed for personal gain, then call them used, broken and throwaways to break their spirit of any hope. It is about surviving, but wishing death would come bringing a new beginning.</p><p>It is also a story of a lonely man who will not speak bc his past is so vile, but reads a favorite book to let the words carry him away to another place, another world not so ugly. It is about a lady who continues to investigate backgrounds of hopeless, ruined men to perhaps save a life, a lady with her own damaged past looking for answers. It is about a fallen priest who wants forgiveness, acceptance.....love, and it is about a white-haired boy who finds a way to be whole again.</p><p>Beautifully written, but also brutally descriptive and disturbing. Thankfully, some do find peace and happiness in the end.</p></span>
  <a data-text-id="17747603871471330782" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1357181182" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Diane Barnes" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7262060-diane-barnes"><img alt="Diane Barnes" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1329773692p2/7262060.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1357181182?book_show_action=true">Aug 12, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Diane Barnes" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Diane Barnes" href="/user/show/7262060-diane-barnes">Diane Barnes</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1357181182" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12689596915880325025">"Even monsters need peace. Even monsters need a person who truly wants to listen--to hear--so that someday we might find the words that are more than boxes. Then maybe we can stop men like me from happening."<br/><br/> This is the saddest, hardest book I have ever read. There are no characters here who have not been horribly damaged by their childhood, or escaping that, by their time in prison. They are on death row for doing unspeakable, gruesome crimes. They deserve to be there. But the language and sty</span>
  <span id="freeText12689596915880325025" style="display:none">"Even monsters need peace. Even monsters need a person who truly wants to listen--to hear--so that someday we might find the words that are more than boxes. Then maybe we can stop men like me from happening."<br /><br /> This is the saddest, hardest book I have ever read. There are no characters here who have not been horribly damaged by their childhood, or escaping that, by their time in prison. They are on death row for doing unspeakable, gruesome crimes. They deserve to be there. But the language and style used in this novel show us the humanity even in the worst of us.<br /><br />It took me 4 days to read this mercifully short novel. I say mercifully short because it made my soul ache while reading, so could only read for short periods of time. I didn't read at bedtime because I didn't want these people in my head all night long. But I couldn't stop reading, either. I'm glad I didn't give up, because the ending was a magical, uplifting, and, yes, enchanting work of art. I will give it 5 stars because, even though I lack the fortitude to ever read it again, this is a novel I will never forget.<br /><br />Thanks to Laura Webber for her high praise and wonderful review of this book. Without that, I doubt I would have finished it, and never felt the hope and beauty it gave me. I'll never take for granted seeing the blue sky, hearing the birds sing, or feeling a human touch.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12689596915880325025" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2275133940" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6579596001972207819"><strong>Heartbreaking saga inside a decrepit prison</strong><br/><br/>This is a depiction of what life is like inside prison walls from the viewpoint of a killer on death row. He, the murderer, has built up a fantasy of mythical creatures to enhance and mitigate the horror that surrounds him, including vicious prisoners and prison guards. Everything about his life is miserable, the dank, lice-ridden cell, the disgusting food, little more than slop, and his own memories of his despicable crime.<br/><br/>This is written beautifully, </span>
  <span id="freeText6579596001972207819" style="display:none"><strong>Heartbreaking saga inside a decrepit prison</strong><br /><br />This is a depiction of what life is like inside prison walls from the viewpoint of a killer on death row. He, the murderer, has built up a fantasy of mythical creatures to enhance and mitigate the horror that surrounds him, including vicious prisoners and prison guards. Everything about his life is miserable, the dank, lice-ridden cell, the disgusting food, little more than slop, and his own memories of his despicable crime.<br /><br />This is written beautifully, and I felt empathy for these criminals. I know that their horrific childhoods made them what they are in many cases, I can't recommend this, though because it's too depressing.<br /></span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('RXmrJLucKJvmkcs9wZe8gxbRsO9jvDaNr+EXCmpg2theCO8VZkvj0tJdluPdd7/clA7IGmTE60QPtfka4oveJQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('SH05EIAXOuv3jVyANFKRv2T9ZCrrkZ+bYOglYEEWTE9TDH0hXcDxosNBAV4ospLg5iIc3+zpQlLAvMtwyf1Isg==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer9387799296854501952">Rene Denfeld is the bestselling author of THE CHILD FINDER, THE ENCHANTED and thee THE BUTTERFLY GIRL, which Margaret Atwood raved on twitter is "a heartbreaking, finger-gnawing, yet ultimately hopeful novel."<br/><br/>Rene's poetic fiction has won numerous awards including the French Prix, an ALA Medal for Excellence and an IMPAC listing. Rene works as an investigator, including exonerating innocents from </span>
  <span id="freeText9387799296854501952" style="display:none">Rene Denfeld is the bestselling author of THE CHILD FINDER, THE ENCHANTED and thee THE BUTTERFLY GIRL, which Margaret Atwood raved on twitter is "a heartbreaking, finger-gnawing, yet ultimately hopeful novel."<br /><br />Rene's poetic fiction has won numerous awards including the French Prix, an ALA Medal for Excellence and an IMPAC listing. Rene works as an investigator, including exonerating innocents from prison and helping sex trafficking victims. Rene has also been a foster parent for 20 years, and is the happy mother to several children adopted from foster care. In 2017 she was awarded the Break The Silence Award for her advocacy work, and the New York Times named her hero of the year. </span>
